Include pod UID in the log
### Is there an existing issue for this?

- [x] I have searched the existing issues

### Is your feature request related to a problem?

_No response_

### Describe the feature you would like

Currently the Tetragon log includes IDs like a container ID. In other observability and security tools I only have attributes like the pod UID as part of the data. So, to be able to join the 2 data sources together, I would benefit from having the pod UID as part of each tetragon log line.

### Describe your proposed solution

I'm not familiar with implementation specifics of Tetragon. Therefore, I can't really propose solutions. Roughly, when enrichment based on the K8s API responses is done, the pod UID should be included in the resulting log as well.

- [x] I agree to follow this project's Code of Conduct

    35	// ProcessInternal is the internal representation of a process.
    36	// nolint:revive // This is an acceptable case of "stuttering" since the name "Internal"
    37	// wouldn't make much sense by itself.
    38	type ProcessInternal struct {
    39	        // mu protects the modifications to process.
    40	        mu sync.Mutex
    41	        // externally visible process struct.
    42	        process *tetragon.Process
    43	        // additional internal fields below
    44	        capabilities *tetragon.Capabilities
    45	        apiCreds     *tetragon.ProcessCredentials
    46	        namespaces   *tetragon.Namespaces
    47	        // The BinaryProperties is not stored into the process, this field
    48	        // will be constructed on the fly when returning these extra fields
    49	        // about the binary during the corresponding ProcessExec only.
    50	        apiBinaryProp *tetragon.BinaryProperties
    51	        // garbage collector metadata
    52	        color  int // Writes should happen only inside gc select channel
    53	        refcnt atomic.Uint32
    54	        // refcntOps is a map of operations to refcnt change
    55	        // keys can be:
    56	        // - "process++": process increased refcnt (i.e. this process starts)
    57	        // - "process--": process decreased refcnt (i.e. this process exits)
    58	        // - "parent++": parent increased refcnt (i.e. a process starts that has this process as a parent)
    59	        // - "parent--": parent decreased refcnt (i.e. a process exits that has this process as a parent)
    60	        refcntOps map[string]int32
    61	        // protects the refcntOps map
    62	        refcntOpsLock sync.Mutex
    63	}
    64	
    65	var (
    66	        procCache *Cache
    67	        k8s       watcher.PodAccessor
    68	)
    69	
    70	var (
    71	        ErrProcessInfoMissing = errors.New("failed process info missing")
    72	)
    73	
    74	func InitCache(w watcher.PodAccessor, size int, GCInterval time.Duration) error {
    75	        var err error
    76	
    77	        if procCache != nil {
    78	                FreeCache()
    79	        }
    80	
    81	        k8s = w
    82	        procCache, err = NewCache(size, GCInterval)
    83	        if err != nil {
    84	                k8s = nil
    85	        }
    86	        return err
    87	}
    88	
    89	func FreeCache() {
    90	        procCache.purge()
    91	        procCache = nil
    92	}
    93	
    94	// GetProcessCopy() duplicates tetragon.Process and returns it
    95	func (pi *ProcessInternal) GetProcessCopy() *tetragon.Process {
    96	        if pi.process == nil {
    97	                return nil
    98	        }
    99	        pi.mu.Lock()
   100	        proc := proto.Clone(pi.process).(*tetragon.Process)

   187	message Process {
   188	  // Exec ID uniquely identifies the process over time across all the nodes in the cluster.
   189	  string exec_id = 1;
   190	  // Process identifier from host PID namespace.
   191	  google.protobuf.UInt32Value pid = 2;
   192	  // The effective User identifier used for permission checks. This field maps to the
   193	  // 'ProcessCredentials.euid' field. Run with the `--enable-process-cred` flag to
   194	  // enable 'ProcessCredentials' and get all the User and Group identifiers.
   195	  google.protobuf.UInt32Value uid = 3;
   196	  // Current working directory of the process.
   197	  string cwd = 4;
   198	  // Absolute path of the executed binary.
   199	  string binary = 5;
   200	  // Arguments passed to the binary at execution.
   201	  string arguments = 6;
   202	  // Flags are for debugging purposes only and should not be considered a
   203	  // reliable source of information. They hold various information about
   204	  // which syscalls generated events, use of internal Tetragon buffers,
   205	  // errors and more.
   206	  // - `execve` This event is generated by an execve syscall for a new
   207	  // process. See procFs for the other option. A correctly formatted event
   208	  // should either set execve or procFS (described next).
   209	  // - `procFS` This event is generated from a proc interface. This happens
   210	  // at Tetragon init when existing processes are being loaded into Tetragon
   211	  // event buffer. All events should have either execve or procFS set.
   212	  // - `truncFilename` Indicates a truncated processes filename because the
   213	  // buffer size is too small to contain the process filename. Consider
   214	  // increasing buffer size to avoid this.
   215	  // - `truncArgs` Indicates truncated the processes arguments because the
   216	  // buffer size was too small to contain all exec args. Consider increasing
   217	  // buffer size to avoid this.
   218	  // - `taskWalk` Primarily useful for debugging. Indicates a walked process
   219	  // hierarchy to find a parent process in the Tetragon buffer. This may
   220	  // happen when we did not receive an exec event for the immediate parent of
   221	  // a process. Typically means we are looking at a fork that in turn did
   222	  // another fork we don't currently track fork events exactly and instead
   223	  // push an event with the original parent exec data. This flag can provide
   224	  // this insight into the event if needed.
   225	  // - `miss` An error flag indicating we could not find parent info in the
   226	  // Tetragon event buffer. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
   227	  // developers for debugging. Tetragon will do its best to recover
   228	  // information about the process from available kernel data structures
   229	  // instead of using cached info in this case. However, args will not be
   230	  // available.
   231	  // - `needsAUID` An internal flag for Tetragon to indicate the audit has
   232	  // not yet been resolved. The BPF hooks look at this flag to determine if
   233	  // probing the audit system is necessary.
   234	  // - `errorFilename` An error flag indicating an error happened while
   235	  // reading the filename. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
   236	  // developers for debugging.
   237	  // - `errorArgs` An error flag indicating an error happened while reading
   238	  // the process args. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
   239	  // developers for debugging
   240	  // - `needsCWD` An internal flag for Tetragon to indicate the current
   241	  // working directory has not yet been resolved. The Tetragon hooks look at
   242	  // this flag to determine if probing the CWD is necessary.
   243	  // - `noCWDSupport` Indicates that CWD is removed from the event because
   244	  // the buffer size is too small. Consider increasing buffer size to avoid
   245	  // this.
   246	  // - `rootCWD` Indicates that CWD is the root directory. This is necessary
   247	  // to inform readers the CWD is not in the event buffer and is '/' instead.
   248	  // - `errorCWD` An error flag indicating an error occurred while reading
   249	  // the CWD of a process. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
   250	  // developers for debugging.
   251	  // - `clone` Indicates the process issued a clone before exec*. This is the
   252	  // general flow to exec* a new process, however its possible to replace the
   253	  // current process with a new process by doing an exec* without a clone. In
   254	  // this case the flag will be omitted and the same PID will be used by the
   255	  // kernel for both the old process and the newly exec'd process.
   256	  // - `unknown` Indicates the process was not found in the process cache
   257	  // and contains just pid and start time.
   258	  string flags = 7;
   259	  // Start time of the execution.
   260	  google.protobuf.Timestamp start_time = 8;
   261	  // Audit user ID, this ID is assigned to a user upon login and is inherited
   262	  // by every process even when the user's identity changes. For example, by
   263	  // switching user accounts with su - john.
   264	  google.protobuf.UInt32Value auid = 9;
   265	  // Information about the the Kubernetes Pod where the event originated.
   266	  Pod pod = 10;
   267	  // The 15 first digits of the container ID.
   268	  string docker = 11;
   269	  // Exec ID of the parent process.
   270	  string parent_exec_id = 12;
   271	  // Reference counter from the Tetragon process cache.
   272	  uint32 refcnt = 13;
   273	  // Set of capabilities that define the permissions the process can execute with.
   274	  Capabilities cap = 14;
   275	  // Linux namespaces of the process, disabled by default, can be enabled by
   276	  // the `--enable-process-ns` flag.
   277	  Namespaces ns = 15;
   278	  // Thread ID, note that for the thread group leader, tid is equal to pid.
   279	  google.protobuf.UInt32Value tid = 16;
   280	  // Process credentials, disabled by default, can be enabled by the
   281	  // `--enable-process-cred` flag.
   282	  ProcessCredentials process_credentials = 17;
   283	  // Executed binary properties. This field is only available on ProcessExec events.
   284	  BinaryProperties binary_properties = 18;
   285	  // UserRecord contains user information about the event.
   286	  // It is only supported when i) Tetragon is running as a systemd service or directly on the host, and
   287	  // ii) when the flag `--username-metadata` is set to "unix". In this case, the information is retrieved from
   288	  // the traditional user database `/etc/passwd` and no name services lookups are performed.
   289	  // The resolution will only be attempted for processes in the host namespace.
   290	  // Note that this resolution happens in user-space, which means that mapping might have changed
   291	  // between the in-kernel BPF hook being executed and the username resolution.
   292	  UserRecord user = 19;
   293	  // If set to true, this process is containerized and is a member of the
   294	  // process tree rooted at pid=1 in its PID namespace. This is useful if,
   295	  // for example, you wish to discern whether a process was spawned using a
   296	  // tool like nsenter or kubectl exec.
   297	  google.protobuf.BoolValue in_init_tree = 20;
   298	}
   299	
   300	message ProcessExec {
   301	  // Process that triggered the exec.
   302	  Process process = 1;
   303	  // Immediate parent of the process.
   304	  Process parent = 2;
   305	  // Ancestors of the process beyond the immediate parent.
   306	  repeated Process ancestors = 3;
   307	}
   308	
   309	message ProcessExit {
   310	  // Process that triggered the exit.
   311	  Process process = 1;
   312	  // Immediate parent of the process.
   313	  Process parent = 2;
   314	  // Signal that the process received when it exited, for example SIGKILL or
   315	  // SIGTERM (list all signal names with `kill -l`). If there is no signal
   316	  // handler implemented for a specific process, we report the exit status
   317	  // code that can be found in the status field.
   318	  string signal = 3;

     6	import (
     7	        "github.com/cilium/tetragon/api/v1/tetragon"
     8	        "github.com/cilium/tetragon/pkg/filters"
     9	        "github.com/cilium/tetragon/pkg/logger"

    20	func getExecCommand(probe *corev1.Probe) []string {
    21	        if probe != nil && probe.Exec != nil {
    22	                return probe.Exec.Command
    23	        }
    24	        return nil
    25	}
    26	
    27	func getProbes(pod *corev1.Pod, containerStatus *corev1.ContainerStatus) ([]string, []string) {
    28	        for _, container := range pod.Spec.Containers {
    29	                if container.Name == containerStatus.Name {
    30	                        return getExecCommand(container.LivenessProbe), getExecCommand(container.ReadinessProbe)
    31	                }
    32	        }
    33	        return nil, nil
    34	}
    35	
    36	func isContainerPrivileged(pod *corev1.Pod, container *corev1.ContainerStatus) bool {
    37	        for _, c := range pod.Spec.Containers {
    38	                if c.Name == container.Name {
    39	                        if c.SecurityContext != nil && c.SecurityContext.Privileged != nil {
    40	                                return *c.SecurityContext.Privileged
    41	                        }
    42	                        return false
    43	                }
    44	        }
    45	
    46	        for _, c := range pod.Spec.InitContainers {
    47	                if c.Name == container.Name {
    48	                        if c.SecurityContext != nil && c.SecurityContext.Privileged != nil {
    49	                                return *c.SecurityContext.Privileged
    50	                        }
    51	                        return false
    52	                }
    53	        }
    54	
    55	        for _, c := range pod.Spec.EphemeralContainers {
    56	                if c.Name == container.Name {
    57	                        if c.SecurityContext != nil && c.SecurityContext.Privileged != nil {
    58	                                return *c.SecurityContext.Privileged
    59	                        }
    60	                        return false
    61	                }
    62	        }
    63	
    64	        return false
    65	}
    66	
    67	func getPodInfo(
    68	        w watcher.PodAccessor,
    69	        containerID string,
    70	        binary string,
    71	        args string,
    72	        nspid uint32,
    73	) *tetragon.Pod {
    74	        if containerID == "" {
    75	                return nil
    76	        }
    77	        pod, container, ok := w.FindContainer(containerID)
    78	        if !ok {
    79	                watchermetrics.GetWatcherErrors(watchermetrics.K8sWatcher, watchermetrics.FailedToGetPodError).Inc()
    80	                logger.Trace(logger.GetLogger(), "failed to get pod", "container_id", containerID)
    81	                return nil
    82	        }
    83	        var startTime *timestamppb.Timestamp
    84	        livenessProbe, readinessProbe := getProbes(pod, container)
    85	        isPrivileged := isContainerPrivileged(pod, container)
    86	        maybeExecProbe := filters.MaybeExecProbe(binary, args, livenessProbe) ||
    87	                filters.MaybeExecProbe(binary, args, readinessProbe)
    88	        if container.State.Running != nil {
    89	                startTime = timestamppb.New(container.State.Running.StartedAt.Time)
    90	        }
    91	
    92	        // This is the PID inside the container. Don't set it if zero.
    93	        var containerPID *wrapperspb.UInt32Value
    94	        if nspid > 0 {
    95	                containerPID = &wrapperspb.UInt32Value{
    96	                        Value: nspid,
    97	                }
    98	        }
    99	        workloadObject, workloadType := podhelpers.GetWorkloadMetaFromPod(pod)
   100	        watchermetrics.GetWatcherEvents(watchermetrics.K8sWatcher).Inc()
   101	        podInfo := &tetragon.Pod{
   102	                Namespace:    pod.Namespace,
   103	                Workload:     workloadObject.Name,
   104	                WorkloadKind: workloadType.Kind,
   105	                Name:         pod.Name,
   106	                PodLabels:    pod.Labels,
   107	                Container: &tetragon.Container{
   108	                        Id:   container.ContainerID,
   109	                        Pid:  containerPID,
   110	                        Name: container.Name,
   111	                        Image: &tetragon.Image{
   112	                                Id:   container.ImageID,
   113	                                Name: container.Image,
   114	                        },
   115	                        StartTime:      startTime,
   116	                        MaybeExecProbe: maybeExecProbe,
   117	                        SecurityContext: &tetragon.SecurityContext{
   118	                                Privileged: isPrivileged,
   119	                        },
   120	                },
   121	        }
   122	        if option.Config.EnablePodAnnotations {
   123	                podInfo.PodAnnotations = pod.Annotations
   124	        }
   125	        return podInfo
   126	}

     1	// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
     2	// Copyright Authors of Tetragon
     3	
     4	package watcher
     5	
     6	import (
     7	        "errors"
     8	        "fmt"
     9	        "strings"
    10	
    11	        corev1 "k8s.io/api/core/v1"
    12	        "k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache"
    13	)
    14	
    15	const (
    16	        containerIDLen  = 15
    17	        ContainerIdx    = "containers-ids"
    18	        PodIdx          = "pod-ids"
    19	        podInformerName = "pod"
    20	)
    21	
    22	var (
    23	        errNoPod = errors.New("object is not a *corev1.Pod")
    24	)
    25	
    26	// PodAccessor defines an interface for accessing pods from Kubernetes API.
    27	type PodAccessor interface {
    28	        // Find a pod/container pair for the given container ID.
    29	        FindContainer(containerID string) (*corev1.Pod, *corev1.ContainerStatus, bool)
    30	        // Find a pod given the podID
    31	        FindPod(podID string) (*corev1.Pod, error)
    32	        // Find a mirror pod for a static pod
    33	        FindMirrorPod(hash string) (*corev1.Pod, error)
    34	}
    35	
    36	func ContainerIDKey(contID string) (string, error) {
    37	        parts := strings.Split(contID, "//")
    38	        if len(parts) != 2 {
    39	                return "", fmt.Errorf("unexpected containerID format, expecting 'docker://<name>', got %q", contID)
    40	        }
    41	        cid := parts[1]
    42	        if len(cid) > containerIDLen {
    43	                cid = cid[:containerIDLen]
    44	        }
    45	        return cid, nil
    46	
    47	}
    48	
    49	// ContainerIndexFunc index pod by container IDs.
    50	func ContainerIndexFunc(obj interface{}) ([]string, error) {
    51	        var containerIDs []string
    52	        putContainer := func(fullContainerID string) error {
    53	                if fullContainerID == "" {
    54	                        // This is expected if the container hasn't been started. This function
    55	                        // will get called again after the container starts, so we just need to
    56	                        // be patient.
    57	                        return nil
    58	                }
    59	                cid, err := ContainerIDKey(fullContainerID)
    60	                if err != nil {
    61	                        return err
    62	                }
    63	                containerIDs = append(containerIDs, cid)
    64	                return nil
    65	        }
    66	
    67	        switch t := obj.(type) {
    68	        case *corev1.Pod:
    69	                for _, container := range t.Status.InitContainerStatuses {
    70	                        err := putContainer(container.ContainerID)
    71	                        if err != nil {
    72	                                return nil, err
    73	                        }
    74	                }
    75	                for _, container := range t.Status.ContainerStatuses {
    76	                        err := putContainer(container.ContainerID)
    77	                        if err != nil {
    78	                                return nil, err
    79	                        }
    80	                }
    81	                for _, container := range t.Status.EphemeralContainerStatuses {
    82	                        err := putContainer(container.ContainerID)
    83	                        if err != nil {
    84	                                return nil, err
    85	                        }
    86	                }
    87	                return containerIDs, nil
    88	        }
    89	        return nil, fmt.Errorf("%w - found %T", errNoPod, obj)
    90	}
    91	
    92	func PodIndexFunc(obj interface{}) ([]string, error) {
    93	        switch t := obj.(type) {
    94	        case *corev1.Pod:
    95	                return []string{string(t.UID)}, nil
    96	        }
    97	        return nil, fmt.Errorf("PodIndexFunc: %w - found %T", errNoPod, obj)
    98	}
    99	
   100	func FindContainer(containerID string, podInformer cache.SharedIndexInformer, deletedPodCache *DeletedPodCache) (*corev1.Pod, *corev1.ContainerStatus, bool) {
   101	        indexedContainerID := containerID
   102	        if len(containerID) > containerIDLen {
   103	                indexedContainerID = containerID[:containerIDLen]
   104	        }
   105	        objs, err := podInformer.GetIndexer().ByIndex(ContainerIdx, indexedContainerID)
   106	        if err != nil {
   107	                return nil, nil, false
   108	        }
   109	        // If we can't find any pod indexed then fall back to the entire pod list.
   110	        // If we find more than 1 pods indexed also fall back to the entire pod list.
   111	        if len(objs) != 1 {
   112	                objs = podInformer.GetStore().List()
   113	        }
   114	        pod, cont, found := findContainer(containerID, objs)
   115	        if found {
   116	                return pod, cont, found
   117	        }
   118	
   119	        return deletedPodCache.FindContainer(indexedContainerID)
   120	}
   121	
   122	// TODO(michi) Not the most efficient implementation. Optimize as needed.
   123	func findContainer(containerID string, pods []interface{}) (*corev1.Pod, *corev1.ContainerStatus, bool) {
   124	        if containerID == "" {
   125	                return nil, nil, false
   126	        }
   127	        for _, obj := range pods {
   128	                pod, ok := obj.(*corev1.Pod)
   129	                if !ok {
   130	                        return nil, nil, false
   131	                }
   132	                for _, container := range pod.Status.ContainerStatuses {
   133	                        parts := strings.Split(container.ContainerID, "//")
   134	                        if len(parts) == 2 && strings.HasPrefix(parts[1], containerID) {
   135	                                return pod, &container, true
   136	                        }
   137	                }
   138	                for _, container := range pod.Status.InitContainerStatuses {
   139	                        parts := strings.Split(container.ContainerID, "//")
   140	                        if len(parts) == 2 && strings.HasPrefix(parts[1], containerID) {
   141	                                return pod, &container, true
   142	                        }
   143	                }
   144	                for _, container := range pod.Status.EphemeralContainerStatuses {
   145	                        parts := strings.Split(container.ContainerID, "//")
   146	                        if len(parts) == 2 && strings.HasPrefix(parts[1], containerID) {
   147	                                return pod, &container, true
   148	                        }
   149	                }
   150	        }
   151	        return nil, nil, false
   152	}
   153	
   154	func FindMirrorPod(hash string, podInformer cache.SharedIndexInformer) (*corev1.Pod, error) {
   155	        pods := podInformer.GetStore().List()
   156	        for i := range pods {
   157	                if pod, ok := pods[i].(*corev1.Pod); ok {
   158	                        if ha, ok := pod.Annotations["kubernetes.io/config.mirror"]; ok {
   159	                                if hash == ha {
   160	                                        return pod, nil
   161	                                }
   162	                        }
   163	                }
   164	        }
   165	        return nil, fmt.Errorf("static pod (hash=%s) not found", hash)
   166	}
   167	
   168	func FindPod(podID string, podInformer cache.SharedIndexInformer) (*corev1.Pod, error) {
   169	        // First try to find the pod by index
   170	        objs, err := podInformer.GetIndexer().ByIndex(PodIdx, podID)
   171	        if err != nil {
   172	                return nil, fmt.Errorf("watcher returned: %w", err)
   173	        }
   174	        if len(objs) == 1 {
   175	                if pod, ok := objs[0].(*corev1.Pod); ok {
   176	                        return pod, nil
   177	                }
   178	                return nil, fmt.Errorf("unexpected type %t", objs[0])
   179	        }
   180	
   181	        // If unsuccessful, fall back to walking the entire pod list
   182	        allPods := podInformer.GetStore().List()
   183	        if pod, ok := findPod(podID, allPods); ok {
   184	                return pod, nil
   185	        }
   186	        return nil, fmt.Errorf("unable to find pod with ID %s (index pods=%d all pods=%d)", podID, len(objs), len(allPods))
   187	}
   188	
   189	func findPod(podID string, pods []interface{}) (*corev1.Pod, bool) {
   190	        for i := range pods {
   191	                if pod, ok := pods[i].(*corev1.Pod); ok {
   192	                        if string(pod.UID) == podID {
   193	                                return pod, true
   194	                        }
   195	                }
   196	        }
   197	
   198	        return nil, false
   199	}
   200

+        // added to the inheritable set by a thread without the CAP_SETPCAP in its
+        // effective set.
+        Permitted []CapabilitiesType `protobuf:"varint,1,rep,packed,name=permitted,proto3,enum=tetragon.CapabilitiesType" json:"permitted,omitempty"`
+        // Effective set indicates what capabilities are active in a process. This
+        // is the set used by the kernel to perform permission checks for the
+        // thread.
+        Effective []CapabilitiesType `protobuf:"varint,2,rep,packed,name=effective,proto3,enum=tetragon.CapabilitiesType" json:"effective,omitempty"`
+        // Inheritable set indicates which capabilities will be inherited by the
+        // current process when running as a root user.
+        Inheritable   []CapabilitiesType `protobuf:"varint,3,rep,packed,name=inheritable,proto3,enum=tetragon.CapabilitiesType" json:"inheritable,omitempty"`
+        unknownFields protoimpl.UnknownFields
+        sizeCache     protoimpl.SizeCache
 }

 type Process struct {
-	state protoimpl.MessageState `protogen:"open.v1"`
-	// Exec ID uniquely identifies the process over time across all the nodes in the cluster.
-	ExecId string `protobuf:"bytes,1,opt,name=exec_id,json=execId,proto3" json:"exec_id,omitempty"`
-	// Process identifier from host PID namespace.
-	Pid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,2,opt,name=pid,proto3" json:"pid,omitempty"`
-	// The effective User identifier used for permission checks. This field maps to the
-	// 'ProcessCredentials.euid' field. Run with the `--enable-process-cred` flag to
-	// enable 'ProcessCredentials' and get all the User and Group identifiers.
-	Uid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,3,opt,name=uid,proto3" json:"uid,omitempty"`
-	// Current working directory of the process.
-	Cwd string `protobuf:"bytes,4,opt,name=cwd,proto3" json:"cwd,omitempty"`
-	// Absolute path of the executed binary.
-	Binary string `protobuf:"bytes,5,opt,name=binary,proto3" json:"binary,omitempty"`
-	// Arguments passed to the binary at execution.
-	Arguments string `protobuf:"bytes,6,opt,name=arguments,proto3" json:"arguments,omitempty"`
-	// Flags are for debugging purposes only and should not be considered a
-	// reliable source of information. They hold various information about
-	// which syscalls generated events, use of internal Tetragon buffers,
-	// errors and more.
-	// - `execve` This event is generated by an execve syscall for a new
-	// process. See procFs for the other option. A correctly formatted event
-	// should either set execve or procFS (described next).
-	// - `procFS` This event is generated from a proc interface. This happens
-	// at Tetragon init when existing processes are being loaded into Tetragon
-	// event buffer. All events should have either execve or procFS set.
-	// - `truncFilename` Indicates a truncated processes filename because the
-	// buffer size is too small to contain the process filename. Consider
-	// increasing buffer size to avoid this.
-	// - `truncArgs` Indicates truncated the processes arguments because the
-	// buffer size was too small to contain all exec args. Consider increasing
-	// buffer size to avoid this.
-	// - `taskWalk` Primarily useful for debugging. Indicates a walked process
-	// hierarchy to find a parent process in the Tetragon buffer. This may
-	// happen when we did not receive an exec event for the immediate parent of
-	// a process. Typically means we are looking at a fork that in turn did
-	// another fork we don't currently track fork events exactly and instead
-	// push an event with the original parent exec data. This flag can provide
-	// this insight into the event if needed.
-	// - `miss` An error flag indicating we could not find parent info in the
-	// Tetragon event buffer. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
-	// developers for debugging. Tetragon will do its best to recover
-	// information about the process from available kernel data structures
-	// instead of using cached info in this case. However, args will not be
-	// available.
-	// - `needsAUID` An internal flag for Tetragon to indicate the audit has
-	// not yet been resolved. The BPF hooks look at this flag to determine if
-	// probing the audit system is necessary.
-	// - `errorFilename` An error flag indicating an error happened while
-	// reading the filename. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
-	// developers for debugging.
-	// - `errorArgs` An error flag indicating an error happened while reading
-	// the process args. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
-	// developers for debugging
-	// - `needsCWD` An internal flag for Tetragon to indicate the current
-	// working directory has not yet been resolved. The Tetragon hooks look at
-	// this flag to determine if probing the CWD is necessary.
-	// - `noCWDSupport` Indicates that CWD is removed from the event because
-	// the buffer size is too small. Consider increasing buffer size to avoid
-	// this.
-	// - `rootCWD` Indicates that CWD is the root directory. This is necessary
-	// to inform readers the CWD is not in the event buffer and is '/' instead.
-	// - `errorCWD` An error flag indicating an error occurred while reading
-	// the CWD of a process. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
-	// developers for debugging.
-	// - `clone` Indicates the process issued a clone before exec*. This is the
-	// general flow to exec* a new process, however its possible to replace the
-	// current process with a new process by doing an exec* without a clone. In
-	// this case the flag will be omitted and the same PID will be used by the
-	// kernel for both the old process and the newly exec'd process.
-	// - `unknown` Indicates the process was not found in the process cache
-	// and contains just pid and start time.
-	Flags string `protobuf:"bytes,7,opt,name=flags,proto3" json:"flags,omitempty"`
-	// Start time of the execution.
-	StartTime *timestamppb.Timestamp `protobuf:"bytes,8,opt,name=start_time,json=startTime,proto3" json:"start_time,omitempty"`
-	// Audit user ID, this ID is assigned to a user upon login and is inherited
-	// by every process even when the user's identity changes. For example, by
-	// switching user accounts with su - john.

+        // hierarchy to find a parent process in the Tetragon buffer. This may
+        // happen when we did not receive an exec event for the immediate parent of
+        // a process. Typically means we are looking at a fork that in turn did
+        // another fork we don't currently track fork events exactly and instead
+        // push an event with the original parent exec data. This flag can provide
+        // this insight into the event if needed.
+        // - `miss` An error flag indicating we could not find parent info in the
+        // Tetragon event buffer. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
+        // developers for debugging. Tetragon will do its best to recover
+        // information about the process from available kernel data structures
+        // instead of using cached info in this case. However, args will not be
+        // available.
+        // - `needsAUID` An internal flag for Tetragon to indicate the audit has
+        // not yet been resolved. The BPF hooks look at this flag to determine if
+        // probing the audit system is necessary.
+        // - `errorFilename` An error flag indicating an error happened while
+        // reading the filename. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
+        // developers for debugging.
+        // - `errorArgs` An error flag indicating an error happened while reading
+        // the process args. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
+        // developers for debugging
+        // - `needsCWD` An internal flag for Tetragon to indicate the current
+        // working directory has not yet been resolved. The Tetragon hooks look at
+        // this flag to determine if probing the CWD is necessary.
+        // - `noCWDSupport` Indicates that CWD is removed from the event because
+        // the buffer size is too small. Consider increasing buffer size to avoid
+        // this.
+        // - `rootCWD` Indicates that CWD is the root directory. This is necessary
+        // to inform readers the CWD is not in the event buffer and is '/' instead.
+        // - `errorCWD` An error flag indicating an error occurred while reading
+        // the CWD of a process. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
+        // developers for debugging.
+        // - `clone` Indicates the process issued a clone before exec*. This is the
+        // general flow to exec* a new process, however its possible to replace the
+        // current process with a new process by doing an exec* without a clone. In
+        // this case the flag will be omitted and the same PID will be used by the
+        // kernel for both the old process and the newly exec'd process.
+        // - `unknown` Indicates the process was not found in the process cache
+        // and contains just pid and start time.
+        Flags string `protobuf:"bytes,7,opt,name=flags,proto3" json:"flags,omitempty"`
+        // Start time of the execution.
+        StartTime *timestamppb.Timestamp `protobuf:"bytes,8,opt,name=start_time,json=startTime,proto3" json:"start_time,omitempty"`
+        // Audit user ID, this ID is assigned to a user upon login and is inherited
+        // by every process even when the user's identity changes. For example, by
+        // switching user accounts with su - john.
+        Auid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,9,opt,name=auid,proto3" json:"auid,omitempty"`
+        // Information about the the Kubernetes Pod where the event originated.
+        Pod *Pod `protobuf:"bytes,10,opt,name=pod,proto3" json:"pod,omitempty"`
+        // The 15 first digits of the container ID.
+        Docker string `protobuf:"bytes,11,opt,name=docker,proto3" json:"docker,omitempty"`
+        // Exec ID of the parent process.
+        ParentExecId string `protobuf:"bytes,12,opt,name=parent_exec_id,json=parentExecId,proto3" json:"parent_exec_id,omitempty"`
+        // Reference counter from the Tetragon process cache.
+        Refcnt uint32 `protobuf:"varint,13,opt,name=refcnt,proto3" json:"refcnt,omitempty"`
+        // Set of capabilities that define the permissions the process can execute with.
+        Cap *Capabilities `protobuf:"bytes,14,opt,name=cap,proto3" json:"cap,omitempty"`
+        // Linux namespaces of the process, disabled by default, can be enabled by
+        // the `--enable-process-ns` flag.
+        Ns *Namespaces `protobuf:"bytes,15,opt,name=ns,proto3" json:"ns,omitempty"`
+        // Thread ID, note that for the thread group leader, tid is equal to pid.
+        Tid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,16,opt,name=tid,proto3" json:"tid,omitempty"`
+        // Process credentials, disabled by default, can be enabled by the
+        // `--enable-process-cred` flag.
+        ProcessCredentials *ProcessCredentials `protobuf:"bytes,17,opt,name=process_credentials,json=processCredentials,proto3" json:"process_credentials,omitempty"`
+        // Executed binary properties. This field is only available on ProcessExec events.
+        BinaryProperties *BinaryProperties `protobuf:"bytes,18,opt,name=binary_properties,json=binaryProperties,proto3" json:"binary_properties,omitempty"`
+        // UserRecord contains user information about the event.
+        // It is only supported when i) Tetragon is running as a systemd service or directly on the host, and
+        // ii) when the flag `--username-metadata` is set to "unix". In this case, the information is retrieved from
+        // the traditional user database `/etc/passwd` and no name services lookups are performed.
+        // The resolution will only be attempted for processes in the host namespace.
+        // Note that this resolution happens in user-space, which means that mapping might have changed
+        // between the in-kernel BPF hook being executed and the username resolution.
+        User *UserRecord `protobuf:"bytes,19,opt,name=user,proto3" json:"user,omitempty"`
+        // If set to true, this process is containerized and is a member of the
+        // process tree rooted at pid=1 in its PID namespace. This is useful if,
+        // for example, you wish to discern whether a process was spawned using a
+        // tool like nsenter or kubectl exec.
+        InInitTree    *wrapperspb.BoolValue `protobuf:"bytes,20,opt,name=in_init_tree,json=inInitTree,proto3" json:"in_init_tree,omitempty"`
+        unknownFields protoimpl.UnknownFields
+        sizeCache     protoimpl.SizeCache
 }

-	// Process identifier in the container namespace.
-	Pid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,5,opt,name=pid,proto3" json:"pid,omitempty"`
-	// If this is set true, it means that the process might have been originated from
-	// a Kubernetes exec probe. For this field to be true, the following must be true:
-	//  1. The binary field matches the first element of the exec command list for either
-	//     liveness or readiness probe excluding the basename. For example, "/bin/ls"
-	//     and "ls" are considered a match.
-	//  2. The arguments field exactly matches the rest of the exec command list.
-	MaybeExecProbe bool `protobuf:"varint,13,opt,name=maybe_exec_probe,json=maybeExecProbe,proto3" json:"maybe_exec_probe,omitempty"`
-	// The security context of the container
-	SecurityContext *SecurityContext `protobuf:"bytes,14,opt,name=security_context,json=securityContext,proto3" json:"security_context,omitempty"`
-	unknownFields   protoimpl.UnknownFields
-	sizeCache       protoimpl.SizeCache
+        state protoimpl.MessageState `protogen:"open.v1"`
+        // Identifier of the container.
+        Id string `protobuf:"bytes,1,opt,name=id,proto3" json:"id,omitempty"`
+        // Name of the container.
+        Name string `protobuf:"bytes,2,opt,name=name,proto3" json:"name,omitempty"`
+        // Image of the container.
+        Image *Image `protobuf:"bytes,3,opt,name=image,proto3" json:"image,omitempty"`
+        // Start time of the container.
+        StartTime *timestamppb.Timestamp `protobuf:"bytes,4,opt,name=start_time,json=startTime,proto3" json:"start_time,omitempty"`
+        // Process identifier in the container namespace.
+        Pid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,5,opt,name=pid,proto3" json:"pid,omitempty"`
+        // If this is set true, it means that the process might have been originated from
+        // a Kubernetes exec probe. For this field to be true, the following must be true:
+        //  1. The binary field matches the first element of the exec command list for either
+        //     liveness or readiness probe excluding the basename. For example, "/bin/ls"

-	// - `procFS` This event is generated from a proc interface. This happens

-	// increasing buffer size to avoid this.
-	// - `truncArgs` Indicates truncated the processes arguments because the
-	// buffer size was too small to contain all exec args. Consider increasing
-	// buffer size to avoid this.
-	// - `taskWalk` Primarily useful for debugging. Indicates a walked process
-	// hierarchy to find a parent process in the Tetragon buffer. This may
-	// happen when we did not receive an exec event for the immediate parent of
-	// a process. Typically means we are looking at a fork that in turn did

-	// push an event with the original parent exec data. This flag can provide

-	// Tetragon event buffer. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon

-	// reading the filename. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon
-	// developers for debugging.
-	// - `errorArgs` An error flag indicating an error happened while reading
-	// the process args. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon

-	// the buffer size is too small. Consider increasing buffer size to avoid
-	// this.
-	// - `rootCWD` Indicates that CWD is the root directory. This is necessary
-	// to inform readers the CWD is not in the event buffer and is '/' instead.
-	// - `errorCWD` An error flag indicating an error occurred while reading
-	// the CWD of a process. If this is set it should be reported to Tetragon

-	// this case the flag will be omitted and the same PID will be used by the

 type Process struct {
-	state protoimpl.MessageState `protogen:"open.v1"`
-	// Exec ID uniquely identifies the process over time across all the nodes in the cluster.
-	ExecId string `protobuf:"bytes,1,opt,name=exec_id,json=execId,proto3" json:"exec_id,omitempty"`
-	// Process identifier from host PID namespace.
-	Pid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,2,opt,name=pid,proto3" json:"pid,omitempty"`
-	// The effective User identifier used for permission checks. This field maps to the
-	// 'ProcessCredentials.euid' field. Run with the `--enable-process-cred` flag to
-	// enable 'ProcessCredentials' and get all the User and Group identifiers.
-	Uid *wrapperspb.UInt32Value `protobuf:"bytes,3,opt,name=uid,proto3" json:"uid,omitempty"`
-	// Current working directory of the process.
-	Cwd string `protobuf:"bytes,4,opt,name=cwd,proto3" json:"cwd,omitempty"`
-	// Absolute path of the executed binary.
-	Binary string `protobuf:"bytes,5,opt,name=binary,proto3" json:"binary,omitempty"`
-	// Arguments passed to the binary at execution.
-	Arguments string `protobuf:"bytes,6,opt,name=arguments,proto3" json:"arguments,omitempty"`
-	// Flags are for debugging purposes only and should not be considered a
-	// reliable source of information. They hold various information about
-	// which syscalls generated events, use of internal Tetragon buffers,
-	// errors and more.
-	// - `execve` This event is generated by an execve syscall for a new
-	// process. See procFs for the other option. A correctly formatted event
-	// should either set execve or procFS (described next).
-	// - `procFS` This event is generated from a proc interface. This happens
-	// at Tetragon init when existing processes are being loaded into Tetragon
-	// event buffer. All events should have either execve or procFS set.
-	// - `truncFilename` Indicates a truncated processes filename because the
-	// buffer size is too small to contain the process filename. Consider
-	// increasing buffer size to avoid this.
-	// - `truncArgs` Indicates truncated the processes arguments because the
-	// buffer size was too small to contain all exec args. Consider increasing
-	// buffer size to avoid this.
-	// - `taskWalk` Primarily useful for debugging. Indicates a walked process
-	// hierarchy to find a parent process in the Tetragon buffer. This may
-	// happen when we did not receive an exec event for the immediate parent of
